## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration is governed by restoring forces (functions of x) and possibly damping forces (functions of v), consistent with nonlinear dynamics and classical mechanics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Forced nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic driving)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent effective stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (polynomial in x with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in x (x**2) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry in restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of x**2 and v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type self-oscillation
- Cubic terms in x (Duffing-type) → hardening or softening spring behavior depending on sign
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Odd functions of velocity (v, v**3) → dissipative forces consistent with time-reversal symmetry breaking
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, conserved or dissipative dynamics

- `-3.39285482994202*x*(0.0780638344630251*|v|^(1/3) + 1)` = `-0.264856...*|v|^(1/3)*x - 3.39285...*x`

The GT has these basis functions:

Now I'll check each candidate. A candidate matches only if it can express ALL five basis functions exactly.

Key observations:
- `|v|^(1/3)` is NOT the same as `v^(1/3)` since v can be negative. So candidates using `v**c` where c=1/3 would give `v^(1/3)` which differs from `|v|^(1/3)` for negative v.
- Candidates need both `|v|^(1/3)` and `|v|^(1/3)*x` terms, plus `x³`, `x`, and `sin(t)`.

Let me check candidates that have `v**c` terms (which could potentially represent `|v|^(1/3)` if the candidate allows absolute value interpretation, but the candidates write `v**c1` not `Abs(v)**c1`):

**Critical issue:** The GT uses `Abs(v)` raised to powers. Candidates using `v**c1` cannot represent `|v|^(1/3)` for negative v, since `v^(1/3)` for negative v gives a negative value while `|v|^(1/3)` is always positive. This eliminates most candidates with `v**c` terms unless they somehow combine to produce the right result.

Additionally, the GT requires BOTH `|v|^(1/3)` AND `|v|^(1/3)*x` as separate terms. Very few candidates have both a standalone `v` power term and a `v` power times `x` term.

Looking at candidates with `v**c2*x` terms (like 34, 65, 71, 82, 85, 86, etc.): These have `v**c2*x` but this is `v^c * x`, not `|v|^c * x`. For negative v, these differ.

Since the problem states v takes both positive and negative values, and `|v|^(1/3)` ≠ `v^(1/3)` for negative v, **no candidate using `v**c` can match** unless it somehow uses `Abs(v)`.

None of the candidates use `Abs(v)`. They all use `v` directly. Since v takes both signs, `v^(1/3) ≠ |v|^(1/3)` for negative v.
